<user>110527055924516348163< /user><user_name>Graydon Cox< /user_name><Date>1511728754430<//Date><rate>1<//rate>< Text>
Service was speedy but that's about all this place has going for it. The restaurant has  changed names but the food is the same basic greasy spoon diner fare as it has been for awhile now. Name change did nothing for the  menu. The tasteful remodel of the old bank building that was done by a previous owner / opperator is cluttered up with old LP records and cheesy Americana signage. One piece is a horribly racist poster of an Asian character with broken English. See photo. The food portion was small for the price and the quality is low. This reboot of a prime spot in downtown Vacaville is a big miss. I hope they try again and get right next time.< /Text>

< text>
I got all my windows tinted a year and half ago, I spent $450 for ceramic tint that is also sun protected. I was assured that the window tints were legal, however, I did receive a verbal agreement that if I were to get pulled over because of the front windows that they would remove the tint free of charge. The tint itself was put on really great. Well, flash forward a year and half later, I received a fix it ticket to remove the front windows. I thought I would have a problem when I did return to the shop and they didn’t remember the agreement especially since the guy who told me wasn’t even there. However, the young gentlemen who heard my version was suffice. I didn’t have a physical receipt, but I did show him the charge on my bank statement. The visit was very fast and pleasant. I don’t ever write reviews, but I had to give this place the credit it deserves.< /text>

<Review>On a trip south from Washington State with a "noise" that did not sound right.  Found Calderon's on the internet and read customer reviews; they sounded positive.  Called to ask if their services possibly included replacing wheel bearings (if needed) and was told that they did.  I drove to their shop a couple of hours later and parked across the street.  As I got out of the car, a man came out of their large building and crossed the street to ask "Are you the one that called about wheel bearings?".  Their best mechanic, Corado, joined me for a test drive on the freeway and initially thought it was a wheel bearing noise.  However, when we returned to the shop, he searched farther and concluded that it was a tire that had worn unevenly that was making the noise.  To prove that it was the tire, they changed it, balanced the replacement and sent Corado out with me to test it.  Corado had correctly diagnosed the problem, and it was fixed!
The entire staff were professional, very friendly and very fast.  Great experience and the problem is fixed at a very reasonable price.  Gracias Corado!<//Review></record></dataset><record>

<name>Rome Sotelo</name><Time>1514700120694< /Time><rating>1<//rating><Review>Horrible...I should have listened to my gut instinct when I didn't see any Korean guests there on a Saturday night. The food was tasteless and the cuts of meat were terrible.  First time going there and customer service was horrible.  I usually don't say harsh things, but they ruined our night. Let's see... they charge for not eating all the meat brought to you, which is understandable... but for the brisket, they brought out nearly 3lbs of meat, which was hard to digest.
Looking past it, they use grates that stick to the food which look like they were bought at the 99 cent store... once the charcoal built up and there was a very large flame... Instead of changing to a clean grill which normal places usually do, they lift it up and add lettuce down below the grill to prevent flare ups. Yes you heard me right,  lettuce.  After the lettuce burned away and another flare up, many leaves of lettuce went down below. We couldn't believe it, asking if we were okay, I asked for a single piece of steak...it never came.  Then deciding to leave, I directly handed the man the water container, and said he'll bring more, but he never came back.

The entire restaurant was filled with Non-Korean customers...and I thought, if they own people won't even eat here this is a bad sign. I felt bad to all the "foreign guests" becsuse this is probably their interpretation of Korean BBQ. Little did they know that they were duped and the experience was lackluster.

Once again, I never write bad things about others... however I feel compelled to warn "foreign guests" to beware of this place.  I wish I could stand in front and tell people not to eat here... however with no wait, with more than enough available seating, Non-Korean guests kept walking through the door.

If you're reading this, don't even try to give it a shot, you'll seriously regret it and be out 36 dollars for the night. Go to Moon BBQ or any other Korean BBQ joint. Don't cry afterwards saying that I didn't warn you!< /Review>< pictures>

<Review>If I could, I would give this dealership ZERO stars!

If you are ever going to buy a used car at Marina del Rey Toyota, be very wary! I responded to an online advertising for a used 2017 Prius Prime that was not Certified. I live 32 miles and would have to drive 45 minutes to test drive the car. So I was texting with their sales person with questions before committing to go and test drive the vehicle. When I asked if the car could be certified, I was told they didn't deem it necessary because people usually wanted to buy an extended warranty (of course this would increase my cost and line their pockets). The car had been on the lot for 17 days, and I thought that was a bit long for a 2017, 9,100 miles and priced at $20,999. I proceeded to ask more questions and eventually decided to make an appointment to test drive.

As soon as my husband and I walked in, we were asked by the sales manager how I was going to finance the car. To which I replied, that I hadn't even decided if I would buy the car. The saleswoman spent a good deal of time with me going over all the features and I took it for a test drive. I really liked it and was ready to purchase. I just needed to walk around the car one last time (it only had a few scratches) and look in the trunk. In the trunk we found the tire compressor kit. When I asked where the charging cable was, she didn't know. We went to her desk and she spent about 20 minutes scurrying around. When my husband complained about our need to get this done, the manager got upset and said they were looking for the charging cable. The manager, the saleswoman and the finance manager came over soon after and told us, "there was no charging cable and we would have to purchase one". Who the heck tries to sell a PLUG IN hybrid without a charging cable? We thought that if we could get the car out the door for the advertised price we would go ahead with the purchase and buy an aftermarket charging cable. But then the finance guy comes back and says he would be losing money if he would include the charging cable in the price. Apparently they would be losing money. Well why would a dealer buy a car and then advertise it for less than what they bought it for?  I don't think a reputable Toyota dealer would do this. They may try to say this with new car negotiations, but used cars? Maybe I'm niave. But this was there stance. We repeatedly asked why they would sell a plug in, without a charging cable and ask that they include it. When they refused, we walked. They let a sale walk over the price of a charging cable. To this day, I cannot understand what went on here. But I suppose the dealer is waiting for some unsuspecting ofe to walk in and buy the car without noticing. The sticker on the car said "sold as is". So if you got home and then realized it didn't have a cable you would be out bucks.

I'm so glad we didn't buy this car, because I now believe that there was probably something wrong with the electric battery which is why it was without a charge when I test drove it.

I will never try to buy a car from Marina del Rey Toyota. They are not reputable.< /Review>< Name>

< Review>
To say I'm disappointed about my experience with Marina Del Rey Toyota's Service Center (as well as Culver City Toyota Service Center) would be a gross understatement. Since I first purchased my Corolla, I have solely taken it for scheduled maintenance to a certified Toyota dealership service center (rather than an outside mechanic) because they "ensure the quality and dependability you trust," as Toyota describes on its own website. Unfortunately, I've discovered that this is far from reality and I would have been better served finding an honest mechanic.

To summarize my experience with Marina Del Rey/Culver City Toyota — I had told the technician at Marina Del Rey Toyota that I was there for an oil change and instead of quoting me for that ($80), he instead insisted on their "basic service package" ($140 after tax) which I later discovered only includes tire rotation (offered free at most tire depots), "cleaning and adjusting brakes", and a "multi-point inspection" in addition to the oil change. Yes, you're understanding correctly — Marina Del Rey Toyota essentially charges an additional $60+ to perform incredibly minor services valued at maybe $20 at any honest repair shop.

But that is not even the reason why I took the time to write this review because it gets worse. I had new brake pads installed / rotors resurfaced at roughly 60k miles. The car was brought in again for an airbag recall at 66k miles and during the visit, it underwent a "multi-point inspection" but there was no mention of any concern with the brake pads or rotors (nor would I expect any issues with new brakes after only 6k miles). However, during my most recent service at 73k miles, I was told that the brake pads were fully worn and the rotors were completely warped, and quoted at $500+ for the repair.

When I made my technician aware that those brake pads were installed only 13,000 miles prior, he told me flatly that the repair was done at Culver City Toyota and thus, I should follow up with them. Essentially, Marina Del Rey Toyota offered zero accountability, ownership, or even basic empathy for my situation. In their words, they told me to go back to Culver City Toyota and "see if they will cut you a deal."

After doing some research, I discovered that Toyota brake pads should last on average 30,000-60,000 miles. Therefore, the only explanation for brand new Brake Pads being completely worn after 13,000 miles is 1) the initial brake service was improperly/poorly performed, and 2) Toyota failed to notify me that there was concern with the brakes during subsequent service visits.

If you've made it to this point in my review, you may simply believe that I am just a negligent car owner who likely drives the vehicle in irresponsible way, and the entire situation is my fault. While I will admit that I should have been more diligent with agreeing to the Basic Service package without more information, I can assure you that I drive with extreme care, especially when it comes to braking. There is absolutely NO WAY brand new brake pads were worn down after only 13,000 miles because of heavy braking in this instance.

WORD OF ADVICE 1: Toyota owners should be made aware that these service centers are all independently owned and managed. Despite Toyota's advertising to the contrary, your quality of service can vary wildly from dealership to dealership and there seems to be no set of standards beyond using certified Toyota Parts.

That means that if you have an issue with your experience at one of these centers and you contact Toyota, they will disavow all responsibility and simply point to this fact. They take zero ownership over the quality of service at these centers which all proudly bear the Toyota name. It's not worth the extra money. Find an honest, quality mechanic instead.< /Review>

Kevin McCormack</name>

Upon return to LA, I went into the Marina Del Rey dealership. I met with their customer service rep Joy.
